<div itemtype="http://schema.org/Review" itemscope="" itemprop="reviews" class="review" id="review_64516099">
  <link href="http://www.goodreads.com/review/show/64516099" itemprop="url" />
  <a href="/user/show/111921-madeline" class="left imgcol" title="Madeline"><img src="http://d.gr-assets.com/users/1220803522p2/111921.jpg" alt="Madeline" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a href="/review/show/64516099?book_show_action=true" itemprop="publishDate" class="reviewDate createdAt right">Jul 22, 2009</a>

      <a href="/user/show/111921-madeline" class="user" title="Madeline">Madeline</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars"><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it">really liked it</span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText"> · </span>
          <a href="/book/show/100915.The_Lion_the_Witch_and_the_Wardrobe" title="Paperback 9780060764890" class="lightGreyText">review of another edition</a>


        


          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a href="/review/list/111921-madeline?shelf=the-movie-is-better" class="actionLinkLite">the-movie-is-better</a>, 
              <a href="/review/list/111921-madeline?shelf=fantasy" class="actionLinkLite">fantasy</a>, 
              <a href="/review/list/111921-madeline?shelf=kids-and-young-adult" class="actionLinkLite">kids-and-young-adult</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer64516099">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer4465207132773242503">Rather than spend this review explaining what I thought of the book, I will instead devote my time to justifying placing this on my "the movie is better" shelf.<br /><br />Reasons the Movie Version Is Better:<br />1. Watching it will take about the same amount of time it takes to read the book, because good lord does everything get wrapped up quick.<br />2. We actually get to see some real fight scenes, and even though there's no blood and it's all very PG, at least it's not just "There was a battle going on but then A</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText4465207132773242503">Rather than spend this review explaining what I thought of the book, I will instead devote my time to justifying placing this on my "the movie is better" shelf.<br /><br />Reasons the Movie Version Is Better:<br />1. Watching it will take about the same amount of time it takes to read the book, because good lord does everything get wrapped up quick.<br />2. We actually get to see some real fight scenes, and even though there's no blood and it's all very PG, at least it's not just "There was a battle going on but then Aslan showed up and it was over yay!" <br />3. The dialogue is considerably less dated and irritating. The kids in the book speak like plummy old British men watching a cricket match in 1800: "'We've fallen on our feet and no mistake,' said Peter. 'This is going to be perfectly splendid. That old chap will let us do anything we like.'" <br />Meanwhile, the movie has lines like this: "When Adam's Flesh and Adam's bone sits at Cair Paravel in throne, the evil time will be over and done." "You know that doesn't really rhyme." <br />4. Aslan becomes much less of a dick when he's voiced by Liam Neeson. <br />5. Since the book is so short (see Reason 1) there's plenty of time for the film to do justice to everything in C.S. Lewis's material, and even add some things. For instance, did you know the Pevensie kids actually have a mother? With a <em>face</em>? Shocking, I know. <br />6. William Mosely is a pretty, pretty boy. Peter the Magnificent, indeed.<br /><br />DON'T YOU JUDGE ME. <br /><a rel="nofollow" href="http://www.imdb.com/name/nm0608440/" target="_blank">http://www.imdb.com/name/nm0608440/</a></span>
  <a onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;" href="#" data-text-id="4465207132773242503">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div itemtype="http://schema.org/Review" itemscope="" itemprop="reviews" class="review" id="review_221362875">
  <link href="http://www.goodreads.com/review/show/221362875" itemprop="url" />
  <a href="/user/show/6610433-midnightfaerie" class="left imgcol" title="midnightfaerie"><img src="http://d.gr-assets.com/users/1318372863p2/6610433.jpg" alt="midnightfaerie" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a href="/review/show/221362875?book_show_action=true" itemprop="publishDate" class="reviewDate createdAt right">Apr 25, 2013</a>

      <a href="/user/show/6610433-midnightfaerie" class="user" title="midnightfaerie">midnightfaerie</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars"><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it">really liked it</span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText"> · </span>
          <a href="/book/show/100915.The_Lion_the_Witch_and_the_Wardrobe" title="Paperback 9780060764890" class="lightGreyText">review of another edition</a>


        


          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a href="/review/list/6610433-midnightfaerie?shelf=childrens" class="actionLinkLite">childrens</a>, 
              <a href="/review/list/6610433-midnightfaerie?shelf=classics" class="actionLinkLite">classics</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer221362875">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer12192790275738634966">The Lion, the Witch and the Wardrobe by CS Lewis is one of the books in his series, the Chronicles of Narnia in which Christianity is portrayed through various fantasy creatures. God, for instance is portrayed as a talking Lion. What a wonderful series! What child hasn’t climbed into a closet and explored the back cracks in hope of finding an entrance to a new and exciting world after reading this book? I used to sit in a closet with the door closed and a flashlight reading my favorite books aft</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText12192790275738634966">The Lion, the Witch and the Wardrobe by CS Lewis is one of the books in his series, the Chronicles of Narnia in which Christianity is portrayed through various fantasy creatures. God, for instance is portrayed as a talking Lion. What a wonderful series! What child hasn’t climbed into a closet and explored the back cracks in hope of finding an entrance to a new and exciting world after reading this book? I used to sit in a closet with the door closed and a flashlight reading my favorite books after reading this series, in hopes that someday a door would open and take me to another realm. Of course, the white witch is my favorite character. I’m always attracted to the bad ones. The Lion, Aslan, is a wonderful character as well, but I have to admit, knowing that he was an analogy for God, changed my view of the story a bit and left me a bit disappointed. He was a bit cheesy. Or maybe typical is a better word. Which is why I almost wish I wouldn’t have known the true meaning of the books until after I read them. <br /><br />In any case, the stories were great, the first one being the best. (You always lose a little of the naiveté of the children as they get older) But the movies did them justice as well. Reading them again as an adult, found me a little bored, but still enchanted overall with the series. The next movie is due out soon and I can only hope they will continue to make the movies which were incredible. I highly recommend this series and consider it a classic as well.<br /><br />Note: I've recently started these again with my 5 yr old and we are loving it. I get to see it again through a child's eyes. And this time I haven't told him anything about the analogy to Christianity, however I do point out certain lessons such as forgiveness. (When Aslan has his talk with Edmund) I want him to figure it out on his own. We had a popcorn movie night and watched the movie together curled up under a blanket a few days ago and as I sat there, I thought to myself, this is why I had children. To experience all my favorite things over again through a child's eyes. It was the best time.<br /><br /><a rel="nofollow" href="http://classicsdefined.com/narnia.html"> ClassicsDefined.com</a><br /><br /></span>
  <a onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;" href="#" data-text-id="12192790275738634966">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

    <div class="section">
      

<div itemtype="http://schema.org/Review" itemscope="" itemprop="reviews" class="review" id="review_563173459">
  <link href="http://www.goodreads.com/review/show/563173459" itemprop="url" />
  <a href="/user/show/18438835-callum" class="left imgcol" title="Callum"><img src="http://d.gr-assets.com/users/1381804049p2/18438835.jpg" alt="Callum" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a href="/review/show/563173459?book_show_action=true" itemprop="publishDate" class="reviewDate createdAt right">Oct 28, 2013</a>

      <a href="/user/show/18438835-callum" class="user" title="Callum">Callum</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars"><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing">it was amazing</span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText"> · </span>
          <a href="/book/show/317500.The_Lion_the_Witch_and_the_Wardrobe" title="Mass Market Paperback 9780020442202" class="lightGreyText">review of another edition</a>


        


          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a href="/review/list/18438835-callum?shelf=fantasy" class="actionLinkLite">fantasy</a>, 
              <a href="/review/list/18438835-callum?shelf=high-fantasy" class="actionLinkLite">high-fantasy</a>, 
              <a href="/review/list/18438835-callum?shelf=contemporary-fantasy" class="actionLinkLite">contemporary-fantasy</a>, 
              <a href="/review/list/18438835-callum?shelf=childrens-fiction" class="actionLinkLite">childrens-fiction</a>, 
              <a href="/review/list/18438835-callum?shelf=christianity" class="actionLinkLite">christianity</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer563173459">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer14037177299777018301">Regardless of the anyone's critical opinion, <em>The Lion, the Witch, and the Wardrobe</em> is one of the most memorable pieces of fantastic literature ever produced (completely disregarding the pop culture influence). Its simple premise, reticulated with a vast allegorically fantastical world remains an incredibly effective method of storytelling, as its themes and concepts still resonate today.<br /><br />The premise of the story is relatively straightforward; four young children are moved to the countryside to av</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText14037177299777018301">Regardless of the anyone's critical opinion, <em>The Lion, the Witch, and the Wardrobe</em> is one of the most memorable pieces of fantastic literature ever produced (completely disregarding the pop culture influence). Its simple premise, reticulated with a vast allegorically fantastical world remains an incredibly effective method of storytelling, as its themes and concepts still resonate today.<br /><br />The premise of the story is relatively straightforward; four young children are moved to the countryside to avoid a war torn London, and are arbitrarily <em>(or so it may seem)</em> entangled into the affairs of another world. However, this isn't just some escape for the young children. Ironically, in avoiding the conflict that afflicts their home, they become the key turning point in another, more elaborate struggle.<br /><br />It progresses in a manner that leaves the reader wondering why they even bother assisting in this vast nearly improbable endeavour, but like any great story, it becomes so palpably apparent without resorting to brazenfaced exposition. His ideas are presented mysteriously, oftentimes are aspects of Narnia hinted or implied, even the grander aspects are enigmatic. They are influenced greatly by the Christian (and other mythological) allusions presented in the novel. <br /><br />This struggle oftentimes showcases common Christian themes such as temptation, faith, betrayal and sacrifice; all of which are basically touted, but unequivocally pertinent to the story. They reveal both the strengths and weaknesses of the four children, their callowness and their ripening. These themes grasp the cast of side characters as well, who are as distinguished as they are intriguing. They are not defined but developed by these themes.<br /><br />Mr. Tumnus, perhaps woven from the story's most infamous image, typifies the challenges of these themes, as do both Aslan and Edmund. Some brush it off as brash allegory, but I see it as a clever, and an even more accessible envisioning of topics which were otherwise bombastic in the hands of overzealous vicars. They were presented as choices, not duties and still preserved the Christian virtue that Lewis still closely follows. <br /><br />So this novel isn't merely a simple piece of fantasy. As familiar themes and concepts are weaved, the story becomes ultimately original. And though C.S. Lewis is very much a religiously devout man, his allusions are presented more passionately than piously. He sprouts truth through fantasy, and at the same time creates an entertaining story.<br /><br />Though the oddities of this quasi-fairytale novel are quite tame in comparison to Eddison or Carroll, I think The Lion, the Witch, and the Wardrobe remains an effulgent presence in the genre. His tale of heroism, his contemporary style blended with a high fantasy splendour both succeeded in telling an entertaining story that didn't falter under heavy themes and concepts. It was both undone and unheard of at the time of its release. <br /><br />Of course, The Lion, the Witch and the Wardrobe holds heavy influence on contemporary works today especially considering the blend of Earth-dwellers placed in high fantastical situations. Thankfully the novel isn't worn with age. Its immensity and broadly-thematic tale remain as rich and accessible as any contemporary fantasy work today. It also remains a model for works of this ilk. Lewis transcends the whims and expectations of contemporary fantasy, and the banality of heroic fantasy. <br /><br />This, more than any other book, holds sentimental value. It was my ingress to fantasy (even preceding The Lord of the Rings and Harry Potter). And the best part is that this novel is more important to me now than ever, as my keenness on fantasy rises so does my reverence for The Lion, the Witch, and the Wardrobe. The subtle aspects becomes clearer, as do the themes and the allegory. It is, irrevocably, an important piece of fantastic literature.</span>
  <a onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;" href="#" data-text-id="14037177299777018301">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer5819653093368463727"><em>"Same here. It's a childhood love. It's nice to see someone write something positive about Narnia for a change! So many people shoot it down for its r</em></span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText5819653093368463727"><em>"Same here. It's a childhood love. It's nice to see someone write something positive about Narnia for a change! So many people shoot it down for its religious themes--I don't quite see why."</em><br /><br />I was also surprised at the amount of people who disliked this novel. I guess the Christian Allegory was the most potent instigator but one must remember that the book is not simply revered for being an infamous Christian allegory. <br /><br />I was around 8 or 9 when I read this novel and the Christian allegories flew over my head. When I found out the story was built on Christian allegory, I'll admit because it's built from a religion I don't follow, I was a bit flustered. But I realized the Christian allegory didn't really ruin the story. Neil Gaiman's views are quite similar to my own, as he says:<br /><blockquote>"My upset was, I think, that it made less of Narnia for me, it made it less interesting a thing, less interesting a place. Still, the lessons of Narnia sank deep. Aslan telling the Tash worshippers that the prayers he had given to Tash were actually prayers to Him was something I believed then, and ultimately still believe."</blockquote><br /><blockquote>"I think, perhaps, the genius of Lewis was that he made a world that was more real to me than the one I lived in; and if authors got to write the tales of Narnia, then I wanted to be an author."</blockquote><br /><em>Lit Bug wrote: "I need to read this! "</em><br /><br />It's a classic that should be read by anyone wanting to get into fantasy (whether you like it or dislike it, actually). And yes, it's children's lit. You'll probably notice a lot of Christian allegory, I would advise not ignoring it, and just make of it what you will. I for one loved how it's based into the story, and while C.S. Lewis isn't the most intellectual supporter of Christianity, no one can deny his passion.<br /><br /><em>"I saw the movies and especially liked the first in the series :)"</em><br /><br />I saw the film as well, I don't plan on watching the sequels until I read the books first.</span>

<div itemtype="http://schema.org/Review" itemscope="" itemprop="reviews" class="review" id="review_1415118991">
  <link href="http://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1415118991" itemprop="url" />
  <a href="/user/show/47862424-becky" class="left imgcol" title="Becky"><img src="http://s.gr-assets.com/assets/nophoto/user/u_50x66-632230dc9882b4352d753eedf9396530.png" alt="Becky" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked &amp;&amp; exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&amp;name=' + shelf_name + '&amp;a=' + action + '&amp;authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('By9AAqOelE92/iS2mpyesonHmNN4JJAxap6JlKA+xAhi+3/RUUyAtfomUA3k/XgAwDBbyjH515sAl4wGbKsyTQ==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {

    <div class=" clearFloats bigBox" id="aboutAuthor"><div class="h2Container gradientHeaderContainer"><h2 class="brownBackground"><a href="/author/show/1069006.C_S_Lewis">About C.S. Lewis</a></h2></div><div class="bigBoxBody"><div class="bigBoxContent containerWithHeaderContent">
      <a href="/author/show/1069006.C_S_Lewis"><img alt="1069006" src="http://d.gr-assets.com/authors/1367519078p2/1069006.jpg" class="right" /></a>
    <div class="readable">
      
<span id="freeTextContainer14722614174968419579">CLIVE STAPLES LEWIS (1898–1963) was one of the intellectual giants of the twentieth century and arguably one of the most influential writers of his day. He was a Fellow and Tutor in English Literature at Oxford University until 1954. He was unanimously elected to the Chair of Medieval and Renaissance Literature at Cambridge University, a position he held until his retirement. He wrote more than th</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText14722614174968419579">CLIVE STAPLES LEWIS (1898–1963) was one of the intellectual giants of the twentieth century and arguably one of the most influential writers of his day. He was a Fellow and Tutor in English Literature at Oxford University until 1954. He was unanimously elected to the Chair of Medieval and Renaissance Literature at Cambridge University, a position he held until his retirement. He wrote more than thirty books, allowing him to reach a vast audience, and his works continue to attract thousands of new readers every year. His most distinguished and popular accomplishments include <em>Mere Christianity</em>, <em>Out of the Silent Planet</em>, <em>The Great Divorce</em>, <em>The Screwtape Letters</em>, and the universally acknowledged classics <em>The Chronicles of Narnia</em>. To date, the Narnia books have sold over 100 million copies and been transformed into three major motion pictures.</span>
  <a onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;" href="#" data-text-id="14722614174968419579">...more</a>

    </div>

      <div class=" clearFloats bigBox"><div class="h2Container gradientHeaderContainer"><h2 class="brownBackground"><a href="/work/quotes/4790821-the-lion-the-witch-and-the-wardrobe">Quotes from The Lion, the Wit...</a></h2></div><div class="bigBoxBody"><div class="bigBoxContent containerWithHeaderContent">
          <div tyle="padding-bottom:15px" class="stacked">
            <span class="readable">“I hope no one who reads this book has been quite as miserable as Susan and Lucy were that night; but if you have been - if you've been up all night and cried till you have no more tears left in you - you will know that there comes in the end a sort of quietness. You feel as if nothing is ever going to happen again.”</span>
            <nobr>
              —
              <a href="/quotes/143080-i-hope-no-one-who-reads-this-book-has-been" class="actionLinkLite">817 likes</a>
            </nobr>
            <div class="clear"></div>
          </div>
          <div tyle="padding-bottom:15px" class="stacked">
            <span class="readable">“I wrote this story for you, but when I began it I had not realized that girls grow quicker than books. As a result you are already too old for fairy tales, and by the time it is printed and bound you will be older still. But some day you will be old enough to start reading fairy tales again. You can then take it down from some upper shelf, dust it, and tell me what you think of it. I shall probably be too deaf to hear, and too old to understand a word you say, but I shall still be your affectionate Godfather, C. S. Lewis.”</span>
            <nobr>
              —
              <a href="/quotes/56726-i-wrote-this-story-for-you-but-when-i-began" class="actionLinkLite">703 likes</a>
            </nobr>
            <div class="clear"></div>
          </div>
        <a href="/work/quotes/4790821-the-lion-the-witch-and-the-wardrobe" style="float: right" class="actionLink">More quotes…</a>
